<Author>coolcaesar
<Content>It's all right as long as you know what you're getting! I stayed at the Embassy Suites Dorado Del Mar recently while on a four-day vacation in Puerto Rico. I read all the recent reviews on TripAdvisor and thus had a good idea of what to expect.Advantages of this hotel include: located in a safe, quiet, pleasant luxury suburb of San Juan; small private beach with breakwaters to ease the waves and lots of rocks at each end to keep out the riffraff; very quiet and peaceful at pool and beach on weekdays; gorgeous, soothing and well-maintained landscaping and architecture; well-equipped fitness center; and wonderfully delicious complimentary breakfast (which is a real cooked-to-order breakfast rather than just continental as at most hotels). All staff encountered were courteous and pleasant.Disadvantages of this hotel: Mandatory 12% resort fee and $7 parking fee (why couldn't that be just rolled into the room rate?); huge crowds of raucous local Puerto Ricans on weekends at the pool and beach who are apparently staying at the Aquatic Club time-share on site; awkward parking situation; the concierge is never in; speed bumps galore coming to and from the main highway (at least eight, I think); cranky computers and printers in the business center; and large but shallow kid-oriented swimming pool that needs refurbishment (it has a few cracked and/or missing tiles here and there).No sign of the Chilean soap opera. Guess they finished filming!As for the room itself, it was well-maintained and clean, with only the slightest trace of a musty smell, and in excellent shape. The bed was warm and comfortable and the furniture looked practically new and in good shape with no obvious scratches or tears. The only major problems noted with the room were a tiny bit of rusting seen on the tiles in the bathroom, a mediocre-quality sealing job on the edges of the walls and fixtures in the bathroom, and a psycho A/C system that seemed to be capable of only various degrees of cooling (cold, very very cold, and ridiculously freezing) and was unable to provide heating or just a straight-through fan. Bring a cozy sweatshirt to stay warm at night.Anyone visiting this hotel in the next year should be warned that the parking lot clearly visible on Google Maps or Windows Live Maps satellite photographs to the southwest of the hotel has just been torn up. The hotel is building a real parking garage (apparently to ameliorate its chronic parking shortage). Unfortunately, this means that you will either have to park in the tandem parking in the temporary parking lot built to the southwest of the old lot, or they will direct you to park on one of the golf course paths on the east side of the hotel, where the hotel employees also park.Also, as many people have noted, try to avoid getting a room facing towards the southwest because that means you will be facing the noisy giant two-story tall air-conditioning unit that keeps the whole complex well-chilled, as well as the construction site for the new parking garage. Fortunately they gave me a room facing the east, so that wasn't a problem. As others have noted, the problem with most of the east-facing rooms is that you don't get much of an ocean view, but that is actually a good thing because the hotel complex is so close to the ocean that anyone actually facing the ocean runs the risk of being kept awake by ocean waves constantly crashing loudly on the breakwaters (at each end of the beach). Another issue is that in the winter, with the sun rising low in the sky to the south, the sun shines on the beach and pool area only from about 7 in the morning to 4 PM in the afternoon. After 4, the pool is in a deep shadow created by the hotel itself and the only area with sun is a small area of the beach at the west end, which gets sun through to about 6 PM.Finally, there's the issue of the distance from the city. Obviously, because the resort is 10 miles from San Juan, you will either have to rent a car or use taxis. If you don't rent a car, you will be stuck in the resort most of the time, which may be a problem because the Embassy Suites is rather small compared to the super-resorts where one wouldn't mind spending an entire vacation (the gigantic Hilton Waikoloa Village comes to mind). If you do rent a car, then you get the dubious pleasure of navigating Puerto Rico's insanely wild traffic. Keep in mind that staying in Dorado outside of the city means having to get up at 5 AM to fight San Juan's morning rush hour traffic to catch a 8:15 AM flight back to the mainland (unless you live somewhere close enough to PR that you can take a later flight). And the morning rush hour in San Juan starts at 6 AM, which implies you can look forward to sitting in bumper-to-bumper traffic all the way to the airport on the last day of your trip. Overall, I had a good idea of what I was getting into (no hotel is perfect), and I thoroughly enjoyed my vacation at the Embassy Suites Dorado del Mar as good value for money. Puerto Rico has the highest homicide rate in America and I enjoyed being able to retreat to a beautiful hotel in a safe, quiet neighborhood at night after exploring the island during the day.But if you need (1) a larger, deeper adult-oriented pool for real swimming/diving, (2) an actual beach for walking, not just lounging around all day, (3) a white sand beach with turquoise water rather than an ordinary brown sand beach with blue water, (4) a hotel that includes all fees upfront in the room rate, (5) a hotel that is in the city, (6) a hotel that is far, far away from the city, or (7) a hotel that doesn't have a crazy number of speed bumps and makes you park on a golf course, then you might wish to look elsewhere.

<Author>dblanken
<Content>Very nice resort hotel This hotel was excellent. The room was very nice, with relatively new furnishings and carpet. The hotel grounds were beautiful, very lush and well maintained. The only thing I didn't like much was the beach area, which was a little dirtier than I expected (bottle caps and other trash occasionally) and the sand didn't extend very far into the water before you met rocks. The trash issue was seen at every beach we visited in Puerto Rico, but it seems like the hotel would take a little better care of this small section of beach. I live in SC, and I have to say the beaches in SC are so much nicer. Also, there weren't a lot of waves due to a line or rocks protecting the cove. Personally I like waves, but this might be pleasant to some. The pool area was fabulous! Also ,the free drinks were spectacular, with lots of selection for good tropical drinks. Also, the town of Dorado was nice, and there was a great grocery store and other shops not far away (within walking distance ~ 1/2 mile). All in all, the place was really nice, with the only thing keeping it from 5 stars being the beach, but I doubt you'll find anything much better in all of Puerto Rico.

<Author>edrub
<Content>Lack of organization I just came back from a class reunion weekend celebrated at the Embassy Suites. The reservations were done around 10 months ago through one of the classmates who volunteered to make all arrangements for everyone participating. When I arrived Friday with my family, I went to the front desk, the employee found my name on the computer, and then I was sent to the Aquarius, which is next door. Finding a parking place was nearly impossible, which is odd considering it is supposed to be the group parking lot. To my surprise upon entering Aquarius, there was a long line. After one hour of waiting in line, I contacted my friend who made the reservations and she said that I was not the only one from the group who had problems with the reservation. She proceeded to talk with the manager on duty, who gave her a couple of different reasons of why they where having problems with the group reservations. After three hours of waiting in line (everyone waiting was already in a bad mood, and also having problems with their reservations), we finally had our room, but I already missed part of the evening that I expected to share with the classmates who I have not seen in a long time. As I met some of my friends they also expressed their problems with their reservations. Some were told that there was no room available and they had to wait until later that day. Others were sent to Dorado Beach, which was at a driving distance, to spend the night and come back the following day to get their room. They waited most of the day and some did not get their room until late that Saturday afternoon. As I was getting ready for our class dinner, I received a call from a hotel employee and was told that their records show that I was supposed to be there for only one night. I explained what happened with the reservations and the group that I was with, and the caller put me on hold for a very long time and never got back to me. The following day we received an envelope with the hotel statement inside, but it did not show the $150.00 that I gave as a deposit for the reservation. When I went to check out, I pointed it out to the front desk employee, and she and the manager had me waiting another hour while they checked. The classmate who made the reservations had to get the copy of my check and reservation document in order straighten the situation. It seems to me that they have to upgrade their computer system, or possibly fire the computer programmer. This will probably save them money as well as keep them from losing more clients.The service on the hotel was OK, but our stay was prematurely dampened with all this reservation problems. Needless to say, my recommendations to friends and family will be poor.

<Author>NeenahGirl
<Content>Best Beach Value We stayed at the Embassy Suites over Easter weekend after a planned check out from the Hyatt vacation club down the road. Hands down the Embassy Suites wins for amenities and price.The great - the protected and private beach was safe even while other beaches in Puerto Rico were closed for unusually rough surf this past March. The pool has a variety of depths and play areas, some are even shaded, to accomodate large numbers with varying degrees of swim skills. Rooms were clean and comfortable with unobtrusive and attentive housekeeping. Concierge desk is helpful as is the front desk staff. Fellow patrons were friendly.The good - Plenty of beach chairs, great breakfast, attentive staff and a family-friendly pool. Clean, spacious and in an incredible complex. The ferry to Viejo San Juan is a short drive away. There is easy access to the highway system and the restaurants in town are gracious and good.The mediocre - Our room reservation was for an ocean view; we ended up in a room that overlooked a parking lot, then a neighborhood and finally the ocean. The staff corrected the mistake after the first night. Ocean front rooms have king beds only with pull out couches making it a tough decision....do we get two beds or make the kids sleep on the pullout for the sake of a spectacular view?The noisy - The open atrium is rockin' until 11:00 on holiday weekends. The suite bedrooms were quiet enough, but the living rooms were too noisy for kids to sleep on the pull out couches. Be prepared to join in the fun.Bottom line - You'll want to return to this hotel.

<Author>Fortwood
<Content>This might be a nice hotel for vacation, but not great for business travelers I stayed at this property for five nights for business. It is somewhat difficult to find the entry since the address does not appear in the GPS, and the map appears on the google map is incorrect. I highly recommend reviewing the direction to the hotel before setting out. The bathroom relatively clean with a few mold spots on the celing. The chairs had lots of stains on it and looked dirty. The room was relatively quiet although it could get quite loud on Friday night when they bring in a band in the evening. The room stayed very cold no matter what I did to the thermostat. The internet connection was problematic. It does not allow VPN connection. I was disappointed in this since they charge for in-room wireless interent connection. The food choices are not so great at the hotel, and I found parking to be very inconvenient and difficult. It seems like most of the guests are having really good time, so I think the property is really good for vacation. But I found it somewhat dissapointing for business purpose. I tried this hotel because it was recommended by the people I was visiting as an alternative to staying in San Juan to reduce commute time, as it will cut down about 20 to 30 minutes of driving if you had to go to the western part of the island.

<Content>Things you should know.... My husband, son  I decided it was time to take a special family vacation - not the typical Florida or Cape Cod excursion. We decided on Puerto Rico and the Embassy Suites. I must say that overall, the majority of the staff at the hotel were very friendly and accomodating. <Author>todebald
<Content>Just poor! This was my second time in this hotel, another 2-week stay. Unfortunately that one was not up to the price paid. I had requested a golf-view room; I got one, nice although overlooking the two huge air conditioning hotel fans which are constantly working and particularly noisy. So I requested another one and was granted a room on the 3rd floor right above the ballroom. Extremely bad location, and unfortunately no other room available! Parties were going on Friday, Saturday, Sunday, Monday etc. with music playing until very late in the night, in fact early in the morning. Terrible when you are there for business. Neighbours in adjacent rooms were particularly noisy, which demonstrates poor room insulation. It was almost impossible to enjoy the pool which did not open until 8am (it was supposed to open as soon as 7am) and would be instantly crowded by hordes of bawling kids. In addition, the internet connection never worked in my room and was never fixed although raised to the hotel staff; and you get to pay for it every day! Breakfast quality is hardly average, and personnel at front desk were overall not really caring. Also, avoid using the laundry service, as my shirts were delivered with damaged buttons! Finally, the food in the restaurant appears to be overpriced; and so is parking. Is that because mid-May was just a bad period? I'm really unsure and was overall quite disappointed. It is unlikely I will stay there a third time, although the hotel location is great.

<Author>4q2
<Content>Dining Options I stay at this property regularly on business. The facilities are good and clean. The pool/beach area is nice. The staff is helpful and courteous. The golf course is not great but very good for a resort course. There have been a couple of reviews that mentioned poor local dining options. I disagree but know the area well. There is a Tratoria (Italian) in the shopping center just outside the Dorado Del Mar gate that is very good Italian food. I don't think those would disappoint anyone and may not be on the hotel list. I'm sure the staff would assist with reservations or directions to any of them.

<Author>OnondagaHill
<Content>Loved the Embassy Suites Dorado Del Mar! We stayed April 10-20th, 2008 at the Embassy Suites Dorado Del Mar. It is a beautiful hotel, with a lush courtyard and nice pool area with several pools. A haven for children! The pool and beach area had plenty of chairs at all times for you. There are some shade trees also to sit under if you wish to avoid the sun.Hotel Room: Clean as can be. This entire hotel was extremely clean. Considering all the people coming and going, the cleaning crew really kept everything spotless. The hotel rooms are spacious, the bed was the most comfortable bed stacked with at least 5 pillows. You can control the air conditioning which was nice and quiet, very comfortable. A mimi refrigerator and microwave was in the room along with 2 tv's.Driving/traveling: You need a car. There basically is nothing to do in Dorado. We went to the El Yunque Rainforest, got lost getting there because we found no sign to turn to Rt 191. I guess someone said there is a small sign that you can barely see. We visited Old San Juan, El Morro Fort, went to Barceloneta to some outlet stores, Arecibo to see the lighthouse/historic park. Paid $38 for the 4 of us. Not worth it at all, plus $2 parking. Not worth it! Found a Marshall's and KMart in a shopping mall near Catano. That was fun.Hotel Parking: They charge $7.50 a day to park your car. The parking lot is in disrepair. It is shared with the golfcourse. Several times we had to park way at the end of the parking lot. I don't mind walking that far, but having to pay for such an inconvenience is not worth it. Nothing you can do.Restaurants: We at at Oregano across the street at the golfcourse. Food was excellent and prices were good. Ate at the pool's Blue Seahorse. They offered nice spinach salads, or Ceasar salads, wraps, nachos, chicken fingers, burgers, etc. Everything we had there was good. The complementary breakfast was fabulous. They offered made-to-order omelettes with whatever veggies/cheese you would like added in. Also offered were bagels, toast, hot oatmeal, pastries, french toast, pancakes, sausage, bacon, cold cereals, fruit: bananas, grapefruit, melon, canteloupe, yogurts, apples and oranges. You could help yourself to tea, coffee, milk and soda. It was outstanding. In town there was a Ponderosa with a nice salad bar, Church's chicken, Applebee's, Pizza Hut, Subway, Burger King. We visited a local seafood restaurant down near the public beach, food was good. Aslo went to a fancier restaurant in downtown. It was pricey, but my steak was awesome.There is a grocery store (Grande) that you can walk to (about 1 mile away). They have everything. There also is a Wal-Greens for any item you may need.Staff: The staff at Embassy Suites were so very nice. You could ask them for anything and they were always most accomodating. If you need directions, the front desk will gladly help you. I can't say enough about the kindness of all the staff, from the front desk to the cleaning crew to the kitchen help to the pool towel people. All were just wonderful. My 10 year daughter really enjoyed Luis who did the children's activities. He was alot of fun with the kids.The beach area: I didn't care for the sand. It was brown and we found 2 nails and other debris including bottle caps and other sharp objects. I would recommend you bring water shoes or wear shoes when you are on the beach. The water area is ok. Don't expect that blue caribean water, it is not.Enjoy your stay here. You will enjoy Embassy Suites. I'd visit here again. I just wish one didn't have to drive so far to get to places outside of Dorado.

<Author>travelingmomOhio
<Content>beautiful location The hotel is beautiful and peaceful. The pool is very big although it was often full of kids. The beach is lovely and there are plenty of beach chairs for every one. The hotel lobby is typical Embassy Suites. The location is far from the hubub of San Juan which can be nice but really leaves you with only a few options for activity unless you want to deal with traffic and waste a good bit of time in your car. Also very limited choice of restaurants and no real shopping in the area. Great golf course though. The hotel has a three restaurants, one closes at 5:00pm, one isn't open on Mondays and Tuesdays, one has a pretty average menu--good but nothing to get excited about. There used to be some casinos in Dorado but they have long since closed--despite what some websites and guide books may tell you. If you stay here you will need a car or really want to just get away from everything.

<Author>sernja2007
<Content>Loved this place, would go back tomorrow We were there for 2 weeks in August and they were still filming the Chilean soap opera! Maybe it goes on forever! It was fun watching them set up the scenes and it did not interfere at all with our stay.Lovely hotel, and the choices for restaurants in Dorado go on and on. We were a group of 7 and ate at a different place downtown every night. All restaurants in town were excellent offering the freshest seafood. Breakfast at Dorado is great, lunch by the pool is OK, dinner, eh, could do much better, go elsewhere. I don't golf, but the golf course is lovely and full of iquanas and birds. There is plenty resort area to walk around and see, they have children's activities and everyone is friendly. Only swim in the marked areas, or sea urchins can be underfoot. Bring your snorkel and some fish food to sprinkle and fish will swim all around you.My only quibble is the location of the massage room -- they have tiny room stuck in the basement in the back of the icey, cold fitness room. It just seems cheesy to go for a massage in a dingy basement next to an underground garage  noisy game room. Come on, Embassy Suites, get with the Spa scene!

<Content>Dorado Beach Hotel We stayed at the hotel for 5 nights. The front desk staff was very pleasant and friendly. The hotel was very attractive. The location is great. When we complained to the front desk they waived our resort fee which was nice, but that didn't really cover the loss of some of our favorite clothes, and some brand new things we had purchased just for the trip. <Author>BigMacII
<Content>Nice Family Friendly Location This is our third trip to the Dorado area: one at the old Hyatt Dorado Beach (prior to children) and the last two at the Embassy Suites. As we have two your children (ages 30 months and 9 months), the Embassy Suites again lived up to our expectations. The family had a great time, as my sons loved the pool area and the abundance of other kids.Transportation: As this location is 45 minutes from San Juan without traffic, I would highly recommend renting a car. Also, the restaurants in the hotel are somewhat limited so it allows freedom of choice for dining options. There are major roadways that resemble the US road and street system. The symbols are the same but the language is in Spanish. The speed limits are posted in Miles but everything else follows the metric system. If you can drive in NY, Boston, or Philadelphia rush hour traffic you will be ok on the roads.Location: Dorado is a sleepy ocean town without much nightlife and no casinos at this time. The hotel is in a gated community in the middle of a golf course. Hotel Facilities: Standard Embassy suites room with added bonus of balcony. We were thankfully upgraded to ocean front/view room on top room that had a great view of the small beach and medium sized pool area (pool side bar, restaurant, playground, baby pool, and numerous lounge chairs). The gym is outfitted with new Precor? equipment and does focus on the aerobic stuff with limited barbells. Also, there is a game room and coin laundry in lower level area. The beach is small but really hotel use only as access to the area is limited. The beach is protected but does get rocky about 10 or 15 ft out from shore.Extras: Happy hour 5:30 to 7:30 and free breakfast is a great touch. The breakfast is a great bonus with youngsters. The General Impressions: The staff was very friendly, welcoming and helpful. It is very family friendly resort (small kids). There are area restaurants and stores for food and supplies, as I will admit the restaurants are somewhat weak. As my son is very picky, we utilized the Applebee, Langhorne (Bayamon), and Chili (near Aricebo) as he seeks familiarity.

<Author>ludlu
<Content>wasted money, vacation...misleading information - awful Given the photos on the Hilton/Embassy website one might assume that the hotel you see is the hotel you get. It is NOT. The right portion of the photo is not the hotel at all -some said it was a timeshare property. The hotel extends behind the wing you see in the photo on the right. What you get on the back side is a view of dumpsters, parking lot and beyond the homes in the distance you will see the ocean. Upon arrival and immediately upon entering the room we were shocked and disappointed. I returned to the front desk and told the staff about my numerous calls and that this was not at all what they described or what they advertised on their website photos. I lodged numerous complaints because in planning I thought I was careful and had personally phoned the 800 number and the hotel itself making sure to clarify what it was that we were seeking. Ocean, ocean view -the beach- we live in a landlocked community and wanted the beach. I was reassured that the room would have at a minimum a partial ocean view and we would be accommodated. The first evening the manager more or less told me too bad, the next morning the am manager offered to move us to the other side. There we looked over a gated community and if you sat in the right corner of the patio the beach was visible. If we could have returned to the airport and gone home w/o $$ penalty- (5 travelers) we would have. We especially wanted to leave after the day we spent traveling on a dry run to the other side of the island to set up our snorkeling and night swim outings. A long trip from Dallas this was to be our big family island vacation. The oceanfront beach offered is a miniscule bay with moss/scum on the bottom of much of the area you can walk. Likely due to the lack of movement within the man made cove. That drive to the other side of the island to do any of the things one might want to do, snorkel, deep sea fishing, ferry to other island or swim in the evening with glowing fish - well the traffic is worse than metro DC, Dallas and any other city we have lived or traveled to and the drive took us 3.5 hours one way. We were advised at the hotel that it was worse during the week. The breakfast buffet was the highlight. The servers wonderful. I have not eaten eggs since returning though. The all inclusive happy hour in California included frozen non-alcoholic drinks for the kids, not here they charged 3.50 or more for them. This is a desolate area of the island and if you want to eat anywhere but this hotel - forget about it. A deli/bakery in town is delightful but that is it. Yes they have KFC, Burger King etc. not what we went to an island to eat and even there you better be bilingual. One of our best vacations was on family business but was at the Embassy Suites in Oxnard, CA. That hotel is beautiful; staff treats you like you are in a 5 star resort. Trust that all Embassy Suites are not equal and do your homework better than I did. Also, be prepared, Puerto Rico is quite dirty and the people are not particularly friendly. Quite a shame. Too many islands too many choices I recommend you make a different selection!

<Author>travelgirl48
<Content>Just Awful First of all, I'd like to say that this was not my first stay at this property. My friends and I were return guests because we'd been so impressed with the property during our first stay. When it opened in 2003 we had been among some of its first guests. We had a great time then and very much looked forward to returning.What a difference 4 years makes. As has been mentioned by a number of reviewers here, a soap opera was being filmed during our entire stay. If I'd been alerted to the fact that the property would pretty much be monopolized by the cast and crew, I'd have chosen another property. There were times when the lobby, the restaurants, the beach, or the pool were not available to us.We also found that the restaurants and larger bar in the hotel closed at 5pm! That was definitely not the case during our first visit. There was no experienced, capable concierge available during our stay. Another disappointing change from our first visit where the concierge was knowlegeable and helpful. Apparently, all their contracts with such vendors as major car rental companies, and tour operators have been severed. We had to rent a car and drive to excursions and sites ourselves. The staff at the pool charged with dispensing towels, cleaning lounge chairs etc., needed more than retraining. They needed to be fired. They were downright rude. When we requested towels the young man on duty said in spanish to his two female co-workers Toallas grandes para las gordas. Translation: Big towels for the fat girls Unfortunately for him, 3 of the 4 of us are spanish-speaking.Add to all that the furnishings are shabby at best, the beach was absolutely filthy and they've added a playground area around the pool for children that was also filthy and needless to say that as a seasoned travel and a travel agent, I'd never recommend this property to anyone.

<Author>Travellfor3
<Content>WHAT A FIND!!!!!!!!!! Our family spent the week of Christmas here and we had a wonderful time!!! We've stayed at the Westin Rio Mar near the rain forest side of the island and also the Ritz Carlton in San Juan another time. We enjoyed ourselves just as much at the Embassy Suites Dorado and at half the price!!! The staff was wonderful and they worked so hard to accomodate you. Every morning there is a buffet breakfast with a chef who will make whatever omelet you want and this is included in your room rate. They offer complimentary happy hour each night from 5:30 to 7:30 with great beer and wine and the bartenders couldn't have been nicer, especially Jose!!!The rooms were just fine, nothing too grand but also nothing to complain about. Most importantly, our king bed wa very comfortable and our 10 yr old daughter said her pullout queen bed was also very comfortable. Each room has seperate bedroom and living room w/pullout and a fridge and microwave. Although we never used our room except to sleep, shower and change. There is a good golf course right on the property and the most beautiful course 5 mins. down the road at the Dorado Beach club that is open to the public to use.The pool is wonderful and the property grounds are beautiful with palm trees and manicured shrubs all around. The beach is small but great for swimming as the water is very calm due to the jetty that is very far out. Food was simply ok, except breakfast which was great. However, there are so many resteraunts around the area that it didn't matter. Definitely rent a car. All in all we would absolutely come back again. If it is a Spa and being waited on hand and foot then this is not the hotel for you. If it is a beautiful relaxing vacation and having to go get your drinks rather than being served them you will love it here. Never crowded and never had a problem finding a chair!!!Also, you get an hour of tennis court time free each day included in your room rate. We paid $56 over at the Westin.

<Author>Phaser
<Content>Good and not so good... Went on a 3 day business trip with my wife and then a 1 day pleasure stay.The hotel overall was nice although it is showing some of its age.Some areas near the hotel were nicely designed/landscaped/maintained. BUT, other areas had a 3rd world appearance, e.g., an employee side entrance/dock and my pet peeve the guest parking lot. Parking was $7/day but guests should be paid to park there! It is absolutely 3rd world atrocious, could never pass in the US especially an Embassy Suites and ESPECIALLY an Embassy Suites that requires paid parking. To go from the parking lot to the hotel required not stepping in sizable potholes, tripping over broken/uneven pavement, soiling and wetting shoes and luggage.Check-in was disappointing--I have been a Diamond VIP for years yet am still aggravated that attention isn't paid more closely to upgrade requests per online reservations...in fact, automatic upgrades should be the norm for Diamond VIP (but isn't) despite my communication to Hilton--too much variability between hotels0. After checking in to the room, I proceeded to go back down and politely inquire for my original request of an ocean view and was graciously given another room but still an unnecessary hassle.The pool is one of the best features of the hotel (NOTE I am not much of a pool fan). It is large and sweeping with 3 different areas/levels with cascading from one to the next, with shade from palms interspersed. Water quality was very good with no obnoxious chlorine smell (which actually is an indicator of possible by-product of bacteria kills).The small beach is fairly nice with great breezes and surf since it is located on the windward side of the island.Of particular note was the entire lack of mosquitoes and bugs. [Let this be a warning--see my yet to be written piece per our stay at the Hilton in Ponce on the leeward side (southern) of the island 2 days later.]The breakfast was typical Embassy Suites level. However, a dinner meal turned out to be disappointingly bad.The manager's reception has booze but nothing of note to munch on, although the Caribbean band set up near the pool was great.The fitness room was being refurbished and I was VERY disappointed in the temporary digs with lack of equipment and not cool enough--only 1treadmill was operating--NO EXCUSE.Our room overlooked the plaza/pool/beach but noise was not a problem. The band usually quit around 11PM. We had problems with a sluggish shower and toilet drain which required maintenance 3 different times.Overall attitude and service was good but not great--I guess I am too used to great attitudes and service from Mexicans (don't bash me, my wife is a Mexican).Getting to the hotel is not easy but was tolerable in my trips between it and Arecibo about 55 miles away to the west.For 3 nights Tue.-Thur. we paid (my company) $139.99 + 7$/day parking + the usual and unusual fees/taxes. Our 4th night Fri. was $149.99 plus out of our pocket.Overall, my wife thoroughly enjoyed her time at the hotel and I did too although I have higher expectations of quality/consistency of Embassy Suites

<Author>azifeyekare
<Content>Ugh.... This trip was not all bad, but the negatives do out weigh the positives.First, you do need a rental car to get around, but be wary of the drivers, because they will cut across a 4 lane highway without signaling once. On the positive, the hotel is very beautiful and we had a wonderful view of the Atlantic. The staff is very friendly and polite for the most part and the cheesecake was to die for. On the negative side when we checked in at 4:30pm, we had to wait an additional 90 minutes because it wasnt ready. They were filming a Chilean soap opera right above us, so every morning we would wake at 7am to banging and noise above us. I have to agree with the other reviewer that the place felt like it was overrun with locals. It was packing with local business people from Merck and the hotel seemed to cater to them first. Several times, the Paradise Cafeteria was closed off to host their events. On Thursday night, the Merck people had a reception in a conference room that we could hear on the 4th floor. When we called to the front desk, they acted as if they didnt know what we were talking about and told us that they checked with the room right below us and didnt hear anything. Hello? Anyone in the lobby could have heard it. So my girlfriend and I decided to get dressed and join the Merck party. Why not? They were too wasted to care. Their was no conceirge the entire week. We had to enlist the help of local waiters to plan our trips to Cuomo and El Yunque. Be advised that the Blue Seahorse bar closes at 5pm. So if you want a frozen beverage or food and you are by the pool, you have to dry off, get dressed and go inside to the Calypso bar. And the manager reception does not include frozen drinks. The bottom line was that this experience could have been alot better. The hotel is beautiful, but management needs to get on the ball.

<Author>MyaOl
<Content>Quick Overview on Embassy Hotel is nice. It a suite so you get two rooms. One is a dining\living room with its on kitchenette (microwave and mini fridge), The other your bedroom. Overall the rooms were clean. Not spotless but good enough.Beach is public so it was not as clean as I would have liked to see it. Although it public, there really no access to outside people. The reason I think its made public is because the hotel is linked to a time share called Aquatics so you get the people from there as well. The beach is very small and narrow. The water was calm. The down fall of the time share is that you get more people than you need to while you are vacationing. Beware that you will get asked to join. If you sit and listen to them talk for about three hours (yes three hours) you get a $100.00 gift certificate to a restaurant and a two night stay at another location. Breakfast is huge. Choice of eggs, bacon, hash brown, sausages, omelets (cooked to order), farina, pastries etc.. Manager Reception, free drinks at the bar from 05:30-7:30pm. Be ready to wait in a LONG line. There is also popcorn and nachos for the kids. Nice atmosphere because it near the pool and they usually have live music.The restaurant across is horrible. It called Oregano and it a wanna be Italian. Great service but not the best food. But hay it was free with our voucher. RESORT FEEAllot of travelers complained about an additional fee on this web site. I learned that if you book through Travelocity it already included in the price. If you book with hotel.com or expedia- the hotel charges you once you arrive. You may want to contact the hotel direct to confirm what carrier charges what.Parking.We had to pay $7.00 a day to park our car. Most if not every hotel I ever stayed at, parking was included. As a guest, I don see why you should have to pay to park your car. SurroundingsYou'll find within a 5 minute DRIVE, a taco bell, KFC, McDonalds, Wendy etc.. There is also a supermarket and a Walgreen within the same distance. Old San Juan is about 30 minutes away and so is the airport.Overall nice time, it all about what you make out of it. So as long as you are surrounded by good friends and family everything else doesn really seem to be that big of a deal.Enjoy!

<Author>SCChuck
<Content>Will stay here again This is a great hotel with a lot to offer. The rooms are spacious and clean. You should have a view of either the ocean or golf course. The complementary breakfast (cooked to order) and manager's reception (free drinks) really added value to this vacation getaway. The pool was very nice, but often crowded and the beach was protected and calm. There are two different hotel restaurants for dinner but one is closed on Sunday night and the other is closed on Mon-Tues nights. The food was good and reasonably priced at both restaurants. The poolside grill was also very good and we found we could share their large Cuban sandwhich and fries and have more than enough for lunch (after stuffing ourselves at breakfast).The only real downside to this hotel is the $65 cab fare from the airport or downtown. All we wanted to do was relax at the pool and beach so the free drinks and breakfast quickly paid for the taxi ride.

<Author>unicorn3
<Content>nice hotel, but limited My wife and I and two kids (22  14) just returned from a week at this hotel. (We encountered several days of rainy weather, but I won't let that affect my hotel review.) Overall, the hotel was fine--room clean, staff friendly and helpful, nice pool. However, there are some definite limitations I wish I had know beforehand. First off, the beachfront is very small, perhaps the equivalent of a block long. Second, anytime you want to travel to the east (e.g., Fajardo, El Yunque), you have to pass San Juan going and coming, and the traffic is awful. Third, there are no water sports or other lesiure activities at the hotel, except for golf and tennis. On the plus side, the breakfast that is included was fine and filling, and the free happy hour drinks from 5:30-7:30 were also much enjoyed. For dinner, however, the on-site restaurants were so-so. In our two visits, it seemed we could either get good food or good service, but not both at the same time. However, the front desk recommended a number of good restaurants nearby. Also, they provided preprinted index cards with directions to various tourist attractions, which was very helpful. For those who are not confident drivers, be advised that driving in PR can be a challenge. Drivers rarely use signals, often tailgate, and love to cut in and out of lanes. On the other hand, we never saw a single accident, so it appears that the natives are accustomed to this style of driving.

<Author>Tripp'sDad
<Content>I'd say average beach resort Due to the new passport regulations we booked this trip to Puerto Rico. Overall the resort was fine. Family of 4 enjoyed a week's vacation of fun in the sun. The hotel was clean and in nice condition although some of the grounds needed better care. Around the perimeter of the resort we noticed more trash under bushes than one would expect. My wife and I were a bit disappointed with the beach because it was so short. We like to take long walks on the beach. The pool area was spacious and we never had any problems finding chairs. The hot tub did get a little crowded on a few occassions, but it was manageable. I thought the pool side bar was a bit expensive. $6.50 for a Pina Colata with rum, $5.50 without. Breakfast and afternoon receptions were perfect.The golf course was in great shape. The adult rental clubs were top quality however they didn't have any junior rental clubs for my son. They did piece together 3 or 4 very old pieces of junk so that he could join me.We took cabs everywhere we went. Typical round trip ran $16. We encountered a wonderful cab driver, Louis Rosado - [--]. He provided wonderful history of the island, culture, buildings and people. He was very reliable. $60 fare from the hotel to the airport. I'd highly recommend his service. We'd call him, or have the restaurant call when we ordered dessert and he be there when we paid the bill.Staff (and infact all locals we encountered!) were very nice.

<Author>egerstan
<Content>The Embassy Suites Dorado, ok but not outstanding We were looking for a place to spend spring break with my daughter that also offered golf. We found a deal with Embassy Suites through AAA. Overall I would say the hotel itself was fine; there is a nice private beach, pretty pool area and the staff is helpful. We enjoyed the breakfasts (more than enough choice) and the poolside restaurant but felt somewhat limited in dinner choices. Because the hotel is so far from the town, not walking distance, you either have to drive to a local restaurant or eat onsite. The Italian restaurant is only ok and the Paradise restaurant seemed overpriced and more than we would want for most nights. But the room was comfortable, the hotel well maintained and absolutely no one was on the golf course. It's about a 40 minute drive into old San Juan and we went a couple of times which was fun. All in all, ok, not great.

<Author>chris92
<Content>Good Stayed there the first weekend in March.The Good:Nice room, great balcony, good pool, decent beach, hot breakfast included, clean.The Not So Good: My reservation said all taxes included  low and behold an 8% tax at check in (resort fee). The reservation was made through the Hilton website. The food at the pool bar  the restaraunt was sub-par. Drinks were around $7 (8oz)  strictly poured. You'll need to rent a car (beware) or take a taxi to do anything outside the resort.The Low Down:I guess it was almost worth the money. We stayed for 3 nights and were definitely ready to go. Driving in PR is nuts. Get the insurance if you go that route  avoid rush hour if possible. If we were to go again, I would get something closer to San Juan or another place that had better choices of restaraunts near by or in the hotel. Though, El Ladrillo was very good. About $100 for two.

<Author>heleneroper
<Content>Wedding and stay at the Embassy Suites I was married at the Embassy Suites on Dec. 8, 2006. My now-husband and I worked with a travel agent who made all the arrangements for us. We had about 50 people come with us for the wedding - and everyone loved it! I was a bit apprehensive after reading the reviews on here, but I can honestly say it was a beautiful, perfect experience. Most of our guests stayed in the hotel proper - and I would definitely recommend that, as the few people who stayed in the other part were not quite as happy with their rooms or service. We thought our room was very clean, very well serviced and had a great view of the ocean. We never smelled anything musty or had any problems. When we rang for something to be brought, it was brought almost immediately. The breakfast was a great perk - and we didn't encounter many of the problems other posters have talked about. The manager's special (2 hours free drinks) was a wonderful way for us and our guests to begin our night. We (and some of the guests) arrived on Monday and other guests arrived throughout the week. We were married on Friday. After our reception ended, the wedding party moved out to the lobby where there was a live band - we partied until 3 am! The only downside was that there was not a wedding coordinator who worked with me on the day of the wedding; luckily, I'm very laid back and was able to work around this. Not all brides would have been this way. We were married on the beach overlooking the ocean and in my mind, it doesn't get any better than that. I definitely believe that everyone who was with us would not hesitate in booking a trip back here. I will say that the weekend got very crowded with kids in the pool, etc, but up until that point it was perfect. Also, a car is probably a good thing to have. We walked to Pee-Wee one night and it wasn't a bad walk, but not everyone would be up for that. We also made friends with one of the taxi drivers and he made sure to assist us, taking different groups to Old San Juan, San Juan, and some of the local restaurants. I would definitely recommend this property to anyone who asked me.

<Author>WanderingPencil
<Content>Dorado Del Mar Was Decent We spent a week at the Dorado Del Mar between Christmas and New Year's. Overall, it was a great way to spend a vacation. The hotel was clean and well-maintained and the staff was friendly and accommodating. Our room was also clean and generally well-maintained. We stayed in a king suite. The king bed was very comfortable and seemed to be fairly new. I cannot say the same thing about the sleeper sofa in the living area where our daughter slept. That was sadly in need of replacement. As a sofa, the cushions were flat and rock-like. When the bed was opened the mattress was also hard and lifeless. Housekeeping (or maintenance) was very accommodating and brought up another sleeper sofa mattress, which helped for the time we were there.The breakfast buffet included with the room was generally decent, really typical breakfast buffet type food, but perhaps could have been warmer. The restaurants associated with the hotel were okay. We ate there a couple nights, when we didn't feel like heading elsewhere. Oregano, in the golf course clubhouse across the driveway, had reasonably priced Italian food and tasted much like a Fazoli's or Olive Garden may. The food at the restaurant in the hotel was okay, as hotel food goes. Not great, just okay.The beach in front of the hotel was pretty nice, but could have used just a little more maintenance. Since some guests apparently couldn't be bothered with picking up after themselves after finishing their food and drinks, there was litter that could have been cleaned up. Maybe if they had a few more garbage cans, people would get the message? But, on the other hand, the pool and hot tub were very nice.The Dorado Del Mar golf course was an enjoyable lay-out, but the sand traps could have used some sand. I expected the traps to be wet, as there was scattered light rain daily while there, but they looked like they had not had any sand in them for a long while and missed the upkeep I would expect from a course that charges $108 a round.As a side note, we made a couple of trips into Old San Juan, about a 35-40 minute drive away in our rental car. We visited El Morro and ate at Buren. I can't tell you what the address was, as we came across it as we were wandering around, but the food we had was excellent and would recommend giving it a try.

<Author>xmascookies
<Content>all around excellent choice My family traveled to Puerto Rico over the Thanksgiving holiday, staying for a week at the Embassy Suites in Dorado. We had a terrific experience. To a number, the staff was warm and helpful. The suite was spacious enough for our family of four. Having breakfast included in the rate was convenient and ultimately saved us some money. The hotel has series of pools, some of which are shaded as the day passes so guests need not be in the sun all day. In addition, there is a small ocean beach with a very minimal undertow, so children and elderly guests are able to enjoy it. Although there are more beautiful beaches on the Caribbean side, this was perfect for a family. Each hour, there's also a short children's program on the beach which is a welcome diversion for the kids and gives them an opportunity to make friends. We enjoyed the hotel so much, we spent three full days just enjoying the beach and pools. We also visited El Yunque and old San Juan which are some distance from the hotel. There are ferries from Catano, which is short drive from the hotel, but they were are in repair during our visit. Driving in and out of San Juan is not for the faint hearted. Give me Boston or LA! Although most hospitality employees are bilingual, others are not. It's prudent to have know at least a modicum of basic Spanish for the inevitable times that you find yourself lost in the city.

<Author>jimny
<Content>OK for families but there are problems I spent Thanksgiving week 2006 with my family at the Embassy Suites in Dorado Beach, Puerto Rico. The hotel is a typical suites arrangement, with breakfast and a cocktail hour included in the price of $235/night. The breakfast food is passable but certainly not restaurant quality. The only food arrangement worth noting is the Blue Seahorse bar/grill at the pool, where lunch is available from 11 a.m. to 5 p.m. The food here is tasty and the portions are large, and an idea is to eat a large (if mediocre) breakfast and then do dinner at the pool bar/grill before it closes.The hotel has a very nice beach and a beautiful series of interconnected pools. There are pool toys and floats that can be bought or rented, and many people simply stay at the water all day. Other activities include tennis ($10/hour) which I did twice, and golf (which I did not do). The two tennis courts are in mediocre condition and not terribly well maintained. Noise is a big problem at this hotel. Once or twice a week there is a band playing in the center atrium until nearly midnight, and there is no escaping the sound. This is an odd situation because there are so many young children as well as several golfers who want to play early in the morning when it cooler. For private events the hotel has a ballroom; be sure your room is not over that facility because the noise and vibration from the music are astonishing and will make you very unhappy.The local shopping is all fast food and typical of low level U.S. shopping centers (e.g., the nearby strip center has a Western Auto), and it is over one mile away. You must rent a car near the airport; do not consider using a limo service to the hotel (as some guests did) because you will be totally stranded. This is a particular problem at dinner time, because there is only one restaurant (upscale) open every night and an Italian restaurant open Wednesdays through Sundays.The best attraction in Puerto Rico may be the rain forest (El Yunque) but it is nearly two hours away past San Juan. The roads and entrances are poorly marked and you should assume that most of a day will be spent going to/from and at this activity. By the way, the directions provided by the hotel were mostly wrong; instead, get a map. Of course, the architecture of Old San Juan itself is fascinating and worth a day trip, although many of the lovely homes have been turned into tourist shops. In summary, the Embassy Suites Dorado Beach is marginally acceptable for the price and for those looking for a family friendly resort. Many of the staff understood this mission; some did not and that made for a few unpleasant moments. If you want sun and water, this may be a reasonable choice. If you want more activities, access to fine dining and culture, luxury or quiet, this may not be your best choice.

<Author>mscuilla
<Content>Great Value The resort is a great place, especially when you take into account what you get for your money! The rooms are great spacious suites for the great price. The pool area is great and real close to a good, not great, beach area. The beach is not as small as other reviews stated. The golf course has a great layout with the back nine being much better than the front. My only comnplaint was they had an outing one day and would not let any guests go out! Saturday morning is very busy and I could not get a tee time early even though when I called from home they said the course would be empty and to just walk on. The course is also over priced, but I guess not for an island resort course. The resaurants at the resort did not look that great (although we did not opt to eat at them), but we got great reviews of other places from tripadvisor's other reviews and loved El Ladrillo and El Marinos. We got a recommendation about a place Alberto's and found it to be average at best. But the other two places were great. The breakfast was awesome. Some people criticized it, I don't know why. They cooked hot omelets or eggs, fresh pancakes and had waitresses asking if you needed anything - just ask for them to reheat your food and it was done. Fresh fruit, cereal, bagels, pasties, french toast, etc... I figure about a $40 value for free. Also the cocktail two hours was great - free cocktails (everything but frozen drinks). Really a nice deal to get a few drinks before dinner and keep from spending another $40 a night at dinner on drinks. We would definitely go back, especially with our yound kids. This time was a nice romantic getaway.

<Author>54kerry
<Content>Good choice for families Our family of 4 (including a 3 year old and an infant) stayed at the Embassy Suites in Dorado in March 2006. We have traveled rather extensively, and were content with our accommodations and the property in general. The room itself was absolutely fine - spacious, with a nice balcony and a water view. It worked very well for our needs. The hotel had a very nice pool area which we all enjoyed, including a nice wading pool for the kids. The beach area was perfect for our little ones, though the lack of waves might bother some. We generally went out and about during the mornings and returned to the hotel mid-afternoon to relax at the pool  beach, which worked out very well - the pool and beach were rarely crowded. The location of the hotel was good in that typically we didn't get stuck in too much traffic when we were headed out (either to El Yunque, San Juan or Arecibo), versus others we know who have stayed closer to San Juan who've experienced a lot of frustration with the traffic. The ferry from near the Bacardi factory made the trip into Old San Juan an absolute breeze (at least once we found the ferry terminal). Our primary complaint with the hotel was the food, as also mentioned in other reviews. The restaurant within the hotel was very bland and uninteresting, and the Italian restaurant across the street wasn't very exciting either (and quite frankly, when in PR I really don't need to eat Italian food). The breakfast was convenient but unexciting - the lack of fresh juices and fruit was surprising. We did venture out a few times to other restaurants in the area, but none I'd really recommend. The most authentic, interesting food we had was in Old San Juan at a little luncheonette called Cafe Manolin - inexpensive, tasty and very friendly service, filled with locals. But we never found anything similar in the Dorado area. That said, if we needed to be in the Dorado area again, I'd return to the Embassy Suites, especially if we had the kids with us - you just can't beat the convenience, and overall we enjoyed our stay.

<Author>tomsak
<Content>Nice hotel for families Just returned from a family vacation to Puerto Rico. 4 of us, 2 preteen girls. We stayed here on 8/1-2 and then switched over to the Westin Rio Mar by plan. See that review separately.This hotel offers what many families have come to love about Embassy Suites...a large clean suite where the sofabed can serve as separate sleeping quarters, the fridge and microwave, 2 TVs. It is a resort but don't expect, well, the Westin Rio Mar.The breakfast buffet is fine, gets very crowded at prime time (9am), but well below the standards of many U.S. Embassy Suites locations in terms of the variety offered. For a Caribbean island, I would have at least expected some fresh fruit (nowhere to be seen) as well as fresh juices. The OJ came out of a mixer nozzle warm and was undrinkable. Add your own ice from a bucket touched by the hands of hundreds. The Manager's Reception was fine and on par with most Embassy Suites. They charge $7 for parking which is a bit much. (Definitely rent a car wherever you go in PR for flexibility and excursions). $10 charge for wireless Internet as well unless you are a Hilton Honors member. The grounds were very nice, good pool, nice clean beach but small and protected by rock jetties. This cuts down the waves for the littles ones but detracts from the ocean feel. However, it is quite a nice setting. There is not much else to do at the resort, no scheduled resort activities. The golf course looked just OK, too hot to play in my opinion. You don't get the trade winds here to the same extent as in Rio Mar which is more exposed to the easterlies. The staff was very nice, friendly and accomodating.About the locals...for a mid-week stay, the place was indeed very crowded at the pool with local Puerto Ricans on vacation. There is an attached time share building called Aquarius which must pack them in and they get to use the hotel facilities. Americans were most definitely in the minority. It does calm down at night.Bottom line, for the slow season, you can work a much better deal at the Westin Rio Mar and experience a true resort vacation. I am just glad we stayed at the Embassy Suites first before the Westin as my family would probably still not be talking to me.

<Author>okislander
<Content>Great for the KIds We had a pleasant experience at the Embassy Suites Dorado Del Mar. We selected this resort due to its close proximity to golf courses. We also were traveling with our two boys ages 4 and 1. The pools were wonderful for the children and the spacious rooms were a plus. The beach was a bit of a disappointment due to the seaweed but the boys enjoyed playing in the sand and we didn't have to worry about them being knocked over by large waves. The free breakfast and the managers receptions were nice and we were always able to find a place to sit. Drinks at the pool bar were very good and reasonably priced for a resort. My favorites were the Mudslide and the Dorado Vice.Now, for the negatives. During the weekend the pools were very crowded with locals, the clientele was not what you would typically find at a resort. On Mondays all restuarants in Dorado are closed except for the fast food. Restuarant choices in the area are limited but we did have a great meal at La Morenas. There is also no good shopping in the area and San Juan is at least 45 min drive. While in PR we did visit the El Yunque Rainforest and El Morro. We enjoyed them both. The rainforest is a bit of a drive (about 11/2 hours). I would recommend visiting both if you have time. According to the golfers in the group, the Dorado del Mar course was okay but they really enjoyed one of the courses at the Hyatt. Although the Hyatt is closed, the golf courses are still open.

<Author>pattism
<Content>Pros and cons... Our overall experience was positive at the Embassy Suites and we knew what to expect based on the reviews posted here. Overall, it was clean, there were no problems checking in or waiting for things, felt the staff was very attentive. The rooms are spacious, very comfortable beds and clean. The daily breakfast was good ( a little too lukewarm sometimes but not bad), some prepared food or you could wait for cook to order. There was a line but it moved quickly. We didn't like that on weekdays breakfast ended at 9:30-my 3 teenagers didn't like getting up that early on a family vacation. Weekends it ended at 10:30. The managers reception at 5:30-7:30 daily was very nice-free drinks...they say 2 but noone checks. Food and drinks by the pool were very good, priced as you would expect at a resort. The pool area is beautiful...multi-level pool with waterfall edge on the beach side. The beach is so-so-it is somewhat manmade as it is lagooned off by a jetty wall. This caused seaweed to accumulate in it once you got 30 feet out so that was a turnoff to some. Not a long expanse of Caribbean beach if that is what you are looking for (if so, go to the Westin--beautful hotel and beach). The major complaint we had with the hotel was that it seemed very crowded with local resident people. Seems like they must use it as a pool club or offer incentive rates during the summer because it seemed to be 90% local residents and 10% visiting travelers when we were there. Made it very crowded and a bit loud.Also, we felt the choices for dining out in the area were not good. Went to La Terrazza, 2 out of 5 meals were passable, 1 was good, 2 were not edible. Other area restaurants were closed one night unless you want fast food. Had to travel to Bayamon for dinner one night. We stayed here because my husband had to work in SanJuan...if we could stay anywhere we would try the Westin next time. Looked beautiful although previous reiews of it were not so positive.

<Author>GROFREE
<Content>April vacation week Found this website extremely helpful in deciding to stay at this property so I thought I would return the favor and post a review. Overall, this property was great. We were there during Massachusetts April vacation week, which also coincided with Easter weekend. We arrived on Good Friday, a major holiday on PR, so a lot of things were closed. Check in had the potential to be slow but my husband is a Hilton Honor member so we got to use that line and it made check in a little quicker. The property was sold old for Easter weekend. It was about as crowded as you could get. We tried to hit breakfast by 8:30 and never had a problem getting a table. Mostly it's a buffet, if you order an omlet or fried eggs, that will be the hottest part of the meal, everything else is pretty much luke warm. Having read the reviews we went to the pool after breakfast and reserved 3 chairs. By noon on Sat and Sun. I'm not sure there was a lounge to be had. The rest of the week was busy, but not like Easter weekend. We ate at El Ladrillo, as recommended by others, and it was a great dinner. Expect to pay $100 for dinner for 3. Our other favorite restaurant was Morena, again $100 for three. Atmosphere was terrific, presentation superb. Take a right out of the gate and take the road along side the Gulf station. We actually ate at Morena twice, picking it as our favorite restaurant for our last night on PR. Manager recommended Las Brasas, Argentinian steakhouse. Don't waste your time, no atmosphere and the food was mediocre at best. PeeWees was a good lunch spot and had dinner there as well. La Terraza was very good, but not as good as El Ladrillo or Morena. Oregano was ok, we went there on our first night. Other restaurant at Embassy Suites seemed to always have a themed buffet for $25-$28. Not a big buffet fan. Never made it to the Hyatt, casino seems to be closed at this point.Ask at the check in desk for a map of the area. They have one with all the local restaurants and grocery store...we didn't get on until about day 5, when we asked for a restaurant recommendation. It would have been very helpful earlier in the week.Bacardi rum tour was fun, better than we expected. Comes with 2 free cocktails.Old San Juan, a good day trip. We experienced a lot of frustration with the traffic. Tried to get several places and got stuck in traffic for 60-90 minutes and would give up. The manager's cocktail hour 5:30-7:30 was more than welcome on those days!Found everyone to be very friendly. Most people spoke English without a problem and were helpful when we forced our 16 year old to use some of her Spanish! I wouldn't hesitate to stay at this property again.

<Content>Loved It!!! Just returned from Spring Break and I have to say that I have visited many places throughout the U.S. but this was one of the BEST!!Puerto Rico is a BEAUTIFUL island with MANY things to do and see. We were only there for four nights and that was definitely not enough time. You defintely want to RENT a car if you want to see other parts of the island getting around can be a bit challenging but be patient. The hotel offers directions to every attraction. But be ALERT because signs are not posted clearly and traffic is CRAZY!!!!Our hotel was a bit distant from many attractions but it was nice to get away from the hustle and bustle of San Juan. Being from a big city myself I definitely did not want to be anywhere that reminded me of home. And yes parking at the hotel is $7 a day but who cares you're on vacation. It's not an all-inclusive resort so don't expect all the perks.The hotel is primarily a FAMILY hotel. So if you are on your honeymoon I do not recommend you stay there. There are kids everywhere. Which was great for us because we have a 7 and a 9 year old. The hotel was CLEAN with a beautiful beach that was very safe for the kids. The pools were GREAT. The restaurants were quite PRICEY but that was expected. It was nice to have the complimentary breakfast which offerered EVERYTHING and it was not crazy at all. We were seated immediately and we always arrived after 8am.The managers special was a TREAT as well. It ran for two hours which was plenty for my husband and I.I HIGHLY recommend this hotel to any FAMILY. Overall it was a WONDERFUL experience my family LOVED it and we would deinitely return.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great family vacation We just returned from our 4 night stay at the Embassy Suites and I can't say enough about it. We went with our 2 kids (2 1/2 and 9 months) and it was a perfect place for us. The price is extremely reasonable and includes breakfast and a manager's reception. The breakfast was more then adequate, I don't know what some people possibly expect. They had everything from eggs and pancakes to yogurt and cereal. We never hit the crowd because our kids are early risers, so we were usually eating by 8:30 am. Besides, you're on vacation, so take it slow!The pool and beach are perfect for kids. We weren't a bit nervous about letting our 2 1/2 year old run from the kiddie pool to the zero entry larger pool. And the beach is so calm that he had his freedom there too. My 9 month old napped in the shade of his stroller and then took a dip in the pool with a floatie we brought from home. You can rent floaties by the pool for $15/day or $5 for an hour. Then we would eat lunch at the pool bar and return to our spacious clean room for afternoon naps (the kids, not us).For dinner, you can order in from Dominoes Pizza or Pizza Hut if you choose or eat in the hotel at Oreganos- decent pizza, pasta was eh. We also took car service to a local restaurant (Il Ladrillo) which was delicious and to the Hyatt Cerromar which has a Johnny Rockets (good for kids) and a delicious Chinese/Japanese restaurant.The manager's reception was outside by the pool. Mostly kids getting free Shirley Temples, but we took a glass (more like a plastic cup) of wine here and there while my son had ice cream from the store in the lobby.We really enjoyed our vacation. Everyone was extremely friendly and accommodating. If you're a family- go, go, go. If you're a couple looking for a romantic vacation- look elsewhere.

<Author>mv99
<Content>A very nice secluded place to stay My wife and I enjoyed our recent (but short) trip to Puerto Rico. We stayed at the Embassy Suites in Dorado for 3 nights. The hotel is relatively new and located in a private residential area on Dorado Beach. It was a nice get away from the hustle and bustle and cold weather of New York City. The hotel is a Embassy Suites hotel - the lobby is open with greenery and waterfalls; the suites are clean and spacious; and though our room didn't have a full ocean view, we could still see the ocean from our balcony which was nice and relaxing. The hotel is very family oriented, so expect kids of all ages. The pool area is really cool and the beach though small area wise was more than enough. Plenty of sun, drinks, and food, they even provide massage service on the beach!!All of the hotel staff, with the exception of the concierge, were extremely friendly and helpful. The concierge was very pushy and tried to sell us hard on renting a car from him. We didn't want to drive during our trip so we passed. My wife and I are vegetarian and the waiters/waitresses at the restaurants were more than accommodating with the lack of vegetarian items on the menus. They tended to our every want and concern. The made to order breakfast is more of a buffet rather than what ever your heart desires, but it's still a nice touch. The Italian restaurant in the golf complex across from the hotel was also very good. We actually ate dinner there two out of three nights. But be aware, it's closed on Monday and Tuesday.The hotel is secluded from the rest of San Juan, from the rest of Dorado for that matter. It is difficult and can be expensive to venture out of the resort if you don't have a car. If going to Old San Juan, I recommend taking a taxi to the ferry port ($35 dollars to ferry port and 50 cents for the ferry) and taking the ferry to Old San Juan. The whole process of taxi to ferry and back was actually very easy, because the ferry drops you off right in Old San Juan. The hotel's taxi driver, Louis, is great. Also, be aware the rain forest is approx a 2 hour drive from the hotel. All is all a very nice and relaxing place to stay if that's what you're looking for.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great experience at embassy suites dorado We were very surprised by the great experience we had here. We usually stay at resorts that are a notch higher that the embassy suites-but the rate/breakfast deal was appealing. We were there w/ our 2 kids-ages 5 1/2  almost 3. The hotel itself is beautiful-grounds, pool area, maintenance, esp. compared to other (older) embassy suites. The beach is small-but GREAT for kids. the pool is perfect for beginning swimmers, as well as non-swimming little ones. The breakfast was always crowded, but managable. the rooms were well kept  perfect sized for 4 people. The other negative is there is NO nighlife whatsoever. There are some great local restaurants where the food was worth it-but if you like to stay up past 9pm-there is very little to do in Dorado. overall, i would definitely recommend the hotel  would return there.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Embassy Suites Dorado, PR- excellent trip We returned from a week at the Embassy Suites Dorado Del Mar, Puerto Rico on MArch 7 ( flight home was a nightmare thanks to Continental, but that's another story) I can't say enough good things about the hotel and staff- it's a perfect place for anyone looking for a low key, relaxing vacation in beautiful surroundings- beach is small but more than adequate if you just like to float around and cool off, pool area was large enough that you could actually swim around without crashing into people and the hot tub in a corner of the pool secluded by plants was never that crowded. The staff kept our room immaculate - i would say to try a room on the upper floor as the weekend entertainment can get very loud- but if you close your inner door, you won't hear it-although there were quite a few families with young children, we must have hit a week where the hotel wasn't fully booked because we were able to find quiet areas to retreat to. Free Breakfast could be busy but that varied and we were even able to grab one of the few tables on the little balcony area overlooking the gorgeous courtyard on several mornings. If you ask the cooks to throw the lukewarm pre-cooked meats and potatoes on the grill as they cook your made to order eggs, it greatly improves the meal-The free cocktail hour was a nice littel break after a day in the sun, sefvice was good and drinks were premium brands. Not for big drinkers though- 2 per person limit- which was plenty for us.Everyone working there, from the front desk to the kids who helped set up chairs and give out towels, seemed to really enjoy their jobs and get along with each other and would help with anything we asked. the restaurant across from the lobby, Oregano, had a good variety, good value and the food was better than we expected. Go into town to El Ladrillo for a treat- the local art on the walls is an extra plus- a little pricey but well worth it.There are stores close by outside the complex - no problem finding things you might need- plenty of familiar chains around.if you go to the Bacardi plant, ask about the ferry in CAtano and take that to Old San Juan for 50 cents- don't drive! the traffic can be brutal and there's no place to park- you can grab a cab once there or walk up to El MOrro-Just be careful if you drive not to miss the turn off as you get close to Dorado- get good directions, as there is no sign for Dorado going west from the airport once you get off the main highway- exit for Dorado is right after toll -if you aren't looking for lots of action on the premises, this is a great place to use as either a relaxing hideout or a central location to travel to other nearby tourist sites. but we found the grounds and hotel itself to be so inviting, we didn't leave to do any sightseeing for 5 days!Don't bother going to the Casino at the Hyatt with the free shuttle - disgusting, smelly and run down- not worth it!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>If you have three kids... My husband and I have the dilemma of traveling with three kids. Most hotels will only allow four to a room, or have suites that will sleep five at outrageous prices. Embassy suites works for us because they allow five to a room. Having said that, this will probably scare away the the couples with no children who want to stay here, and it probably should. This place is loaded with children and teenagers! We spent eight days feb 20- feb 28th and we had a great time. The pools and grounds were really clean and we found the staff to be very friendly and helpful. The rooms could use a little sprucing up, the carpet and sofa were a little worn, but overall it was very clean, no mold or mildew etc. There really is no night life (the weekends have loud music in the center atrium you might want to ask for a high floor) or tons of things to do which is exactly what we wanted. We wanted a vacation where we could just hang out, relax and connect with our children and that is exactly what we got. I strongly suggest that anyone staying here for an extended time rent a car. Parking was never a problem for us, $7/day, we always found a spot. The walk to town (fast food, Walgreens, grande supermarket) is about a mile. We loaded up our cooler for the beach and refrigerator in our room and we bought snacks for the room and for hanging out on our terrace overlooking the ocean. By the way, the ocean is not the turquoise blue that you will see on other islands in the Carribean, not a big deal to our family but thought it was worth mentioning. Also, the ocean is more like a lagoon, very calm because of the rock jetties in front of it, which is great for younger children. If you want crashing waves, you won't get them here. There are sea urchins, I would definitely think of bringing water shoes. I felt the resort was safe, gated community, lots of friendly security staff, and we saw a lot of police presence in town(not needed, just patrolling). The complimentary breakfast was crowded but not crazy, and not horrible (how can you ruin an omelet?). The complimentary cocktails and snacks were great if you felt like winding down with a drink, you could drink them by the pool or inside the cocktail lounge. The pool grounds can get a little crazy on the weekends, the local owners come and stay with their families, but it was by no means out of control. The weekdays are just more quieter. I would definitely consider staying here again, I hope this review was helpful!  
<Date>Mar 3, 2006
